I've uploaded a python code repository in the directory /testbed. Consider the following PR description:

<pr_description>
timeout: on receiving TERM signal, child process is not terminated
(test system: WSL2, Ubuntu 24.04 - also reproducible in github codespaces)


gnu coreutils behavior is that child process is terminated when receiving TERM signal:
```
$ timeout 42 sleep 42 &
[1] 16343
$ ps -ef |grep sleep
martin     16343    3426  0 17:04 pts/5    00:00:00 timeout 42 sleep 42
martin     16345   16343  0 17:04 pts/5    00:00:00 sleep 42
$ kill 16343
[1]+  Terminated              timeout 42 sleep 42
$ ps -ef |grep sleep
```

with timeout from uutils
```
$ target/debug/coreutils timeout 42 sleep 42 &
[1] 16507
$ ps -ef |grep sleep
martin     16507    3426  0 17:04 pts/5    00:00:00 target/debug/coreutils timeout 42 sleep 42
martin     16509   16507  0 17:04 pts/5    00:00:00 sleep 42
$ kill 16507
[1]+  Terminated              target/debug/coreutils timeout 42 sleep 42
$ ps -ef |grep sleep
martin     16509    2710  0 17:04 pts/5    00:00:00 sleep 42
```
the child process `sleep 42` is still running and parent PID is now `2710`:
```
$ ps -ef |grep 2710
root        2710    2709  0 16:52 ?        00:00:00 /init
```


I saw this behavior when debugging sporadic failures in gnu compatibility tests. 
The test `tests/tail/inotify-rotate.sh` needs the termination of child process for cleanup. 
Otherwise a lot of `tail` processes remain alive after the tests are finished:
```
martin     44860    2710  2 17:12 pts/5    00:00:00 tail -s.1 --max-unchanged-stats=1 -F k
martin     44876    2710  3 17:12 pts/5    00:00:00 tail -s.1 --max-unchanged-stats=1 -F k
martin     44891    2710  3 17:12 pts/5    00:00:00 tail -s.1 --max-unchanged-stats=1 -F k
...
```
and with the next test runs I observe messages like `tail: inotify cannot be used, reverting to polling: Too many open files`.




</pr_description>

    29	
    30	pub mod options {
    31	    pub static FOREGROUND: &str = "foreground";
    32	    pub static KILL_AFTER: &str = "kill-after";
    33	    pub static SIGNAL: &str = "signal";
    34	    pub static PRESERVE_STATUS: &str = "preserve-status";
    35	    pub static VERBOSE: &str = "verbose";
    36	
    37	    // Positional args.
    38	    pub static DURATION: &str = "duration";
    39	    pub static COMMAND: &str = "command";
    40	}
    41	
    42	struct Config {
    43	    foreground: bool,
    44	    kill_after: Option<Duration>,
    45	    signal: usize,
    46	    duration: Duration,
    47	    preserve_status: bool,
    48	    verbose: bool,
    49	
    50	    command: Vec<String>,
    51	}
    52	
    53	impl Config {
    54	    fn from(options: &clap::ArgMatches) -> UResult<Self> {
    55	        let signal = match options.get_one::<String>(options::SIGNAL) {
    56	            Some(signal_) => {
    57	                let signal_result = signal_by_name_or_value(signal_);
    58	                match signal_result {
    59	                    None => {
    60	                        return Err(UUsageError::new(
    61	                            ExitStatus::TimeoutFailed.into(),
    62	                            get_message_with_args(
    63	                                "timeout-error-invalid-signal",
    64	                                HashMap::from([(
    65	                                    "signal".to_string(),
    66	                                    signal_.quote().to_string(),
    67	                                )]),
    68	                            ),
    69	                        ));
    70	                    }
    71	                    Some(signal_value) => signal_value,
    72	                }
    73	            }
    74	            _ => signal_by_name_or_value("TERM").unwrap(),
    75	        };
    76	
    77	        let kill_after = match options.get_one::<String>(options::KILL_AFTER) {
    78	            None => None,
    79	            Some(kill_after) => match parse_time::from_str(kill_after, true) {
    80	                Ok(k) => Some(k),
    81	                Err(err) => return Err(UUsageError::new(ExitStatus::TimeoutFailed.into(), err)),
    82	            },
    83	        };
    84	
    85	        let duration =
    86	            parse_time::from_str(options.get_one::<String>(options::DURATION).unwrap(), true)
    87	                .map_err(|err| UUsageError::new(ExitStatus::TimeoutFailed.into(), err))?;
    88	
    89	        let preserve_status: bool = options.get_flag(options::PRESERVE_STATUS);
    90	        let foreground = options.get_flag(options::FOREGROUND);
    91	        let verbose = options.get_flag(options::VERBOSE);
    92	
    93	        let command = options
    94	            .get_many::<String>(options::COMMAND)
    95	            .unwrap()
    96	            .map(String::from)
    97	            .collect::<Vec<_>>();
    98	
    99	        Ok(Self {
   100	            foreground,
   101	            kill_after,
   102	            signal,
   103	            duration,
   104	            preserve_status,
   105	            verbose,
   106	            command,
   107	        })
   108	    }
   109	}

   111	#[uucore::main]
   112	pub fn uumain(args: impl uucore::Args) -> UResult<()> {
   113	    let matches = uu_app().try_get_matches_from(args).with_exit_code(125)?;
   114	
   115	    let config = Config::from(&matches)?;
   116	    timeout(
   117	        &config.command,
   118	        config.duration,
   119	        config.signal,
   120	        config.kill_after,
   121	        config.foreground,
   122	        config.preserve_status,
   123	        config.verbose,
   124	    )
   125	}

   177	/// Remove pre-existing SIGCHLD handlers that would make waiting for the child's exit code fail.
   178	fn unblock_sigchld() {
   179	    unsafe {
   180	        nix::sys::signal::signal(
   181	            nix::sys::signal::Signal::SIGCHLD,
   182	            nix::sys::signal::SigHandler::SigDfl,
   183	        )
   184	        .unwrap();
   185	    }
   186	}
   187	
   188	/// Report that a signal is being sent if the verbose flag is set.
   189	fn report_if_verbose(signal: usize, cmd: &str, verbose: bool) {
   190	    if verbose {
   191	        let s = signal_name_by_value(signal).unwrap();
   192	        show_error!(
   193	            "{}",
   194	            get_message_with_args(
   195	                "timeout-verbose-sending-signal",
   196	                HashMap::from([
   197	                    ("signal".to_string(), s.to_string()),
   198	                    ("command".to_string(), cmd.quote().to_string())
   199	                ])
   200	            )
   201	        );
   202	    }
   203	}
   204	
   205	fn send_signal(process: &mut Child, signal: usize, foreground: bool) {
   206	    // NOTE: GNU timeout doesn't check for errors of signal.
   207	    // The subprocess might have exited just after the timeout.
   208	    // Sending a signal now would return "No such process", but we should still try to kill the children.
   209	    if foreground {
   210	        let _ = process.send_signal(signal);
   211	    } else {
   212	        let _ = process.send_signal_group(signal);
   213	        let kill_signal = signal_by_name_or_value("KILL").unwrap();
   214	        let continued_signal = signal_by_name_or_value("CONT").unwrap();
   215	        if signal != kill_signal && signal != continued_signal {
   216	            _ = process.send_signal_group(continued_signal);
   217	        }
   218	    }
   219	}
   220	
   221	/// Wait for a child process and send a kill signal if it does not terminate.
   222	///
   223	/// This function waits for the child `process` for the time period
   224	/// given by `duration`. If the child process does not terminate
   225	/// within that time, we send the `SIGKILL` signal to it. If `verbose`
   226	/// is `true`, then a message is printed to `stderr` when that
   227	/// happens.
   228	///
   229	/// If the child process terminates within the given time period and
   230	/// `preserve_status` is `true`, then the status code of the child
   231	/// process is returned. If the child process terminates within the
   232	/// given time period and `preserve_status` is `false`, then 124 is
   233	/// returned. If the child does not terminate within the time period,
   234	/// then 137 is returned. Finally, if there is an error while waiting
   235	/// for the child process to terminate, then 124 is returned.
   236	///
   237	/// # Errors
   238	///
   239	/// If there is a problem sending the `SIGKILL` signal or waiting for
   240	/// the process after that signal is sent.
   241	fn wait_or_kill_process(
   242	    process: &mut Child,
   243	    cmd: &str,
   244	    duration: Duration,
   245	    preserve_status: bool,
   246	    foreground: bool,
   247	    verbose: bool,
   248	) -> std::io::Result<i32> {
   249	    match process.wait_or_timeout(duration) {
   250	        Ok(Some(status)) => {
   251	            if preserve_status {
   252	                Ok(status.code().unwrap_or_else(|| status.signal().unwrap()))
   253	            } else {
   254	                Ok(ExitStatus::TimeoutFailed.into())
   255	            }
   256	        }
   257	        Ok(None) => {
   258	            let signal = signal_by_name_or_value("KILL").unwrap();
   259	            report_if_verbose(signal, cmd, verbose);
   260	            send_signal(process, signal, foreground);
   261	            process.wait()?;
   262	            Ok(ExitStatus::SignalSent(signal).into())
   263	        }
   264	        Err(_) => Ok(ExitStatus::WaitingFailed.into()),
   265	    }
   266	}
   267	
   268	#[cfg(unix)]
   269	fn preserve_signal_info(signal: libc::c_int) -> libc::c_int {
   270	    // This is needed because timeout is expected to preserve the exit
   271	    // status of its child. It is not the case that utilities have a
   272	    // single simple exit code, that's an illusion some shells
   273	    // provide.  Instead exit status is really two numbers:
   274	    //
   275	    //  - An exit code if the program ran to completion
   276	    //
   277	    //  - A signal number if the program was terminated by a signal
   278	    //
   279	    // The easiest way to preserve the latter seems to be to kill
   280	    // ourselves with whatever signal our child exited with, which is
   281	    // what the following is intended to accomplish.
   282	    unsafe {
   283	        libc::kill(libc::getpid(), signal);
   284	    }
   285	    signal
   286	}
   287	
   288	#[cfg(not(unix))]
   289	fn preserve_signal_info(signal: libc::c_int) -> libc::c_int {
   290	    // Do nothing
   291	    signal
   292	}
   293	
   294	/// TODO: Improve exit codes, and make them consistent with the GNU Coreutils exit codes.
   295	fn timeout(
   296	    cmd: &[String],
   297	    duration: Duration,
   298	    signal: usize,
   299	    kill_after: Option<Duration>,
   300	    foreground: bool,
   301	    preserve_status: bool,
   302	    verbose: bool,
   303	) -> UResult<()> {
   304	    if !foreground {
   305	        unsafe { libc::setpgid(0, 0) };
   306	    }
   307	    #[cfg(unix)]
   308	    enable_pipe_errors()?;
   309	
   310	    let process = &mut process::Command::new(&cmd[0])
   311	        .args(&cmd[1..])
   312	        .stdin(Stdio::inherit())
   313	        .stdout(Stdio::inherit())
   314	        .stderr(Stdio::inherit())
   315	        .spawn()
   316	        .map_err(|err| {
   317	            let status_code = if err.kind() == ErrorKind::NotFound {
   318	                // FIXME: not sure which to use
   319	                127
   320	            } else {
   321	                // FIXME: this may not be 100% correct...
   322	                126
   323	            };
   324	            USimpleError::new(
   325	                status_code,
   326	                get_message_with_args(
   327	                    "timeout-error-failed-to-execute-process",
   328	                    HashMap::from([("error".to_string(), err.to_string())]),
   329	                ),
   330	            )
   331	        })?;
   332	    unblock_sigchld();
   333	    // Wait for the child process for the specified time period.
   334	    //
   335	    // If the process exits within the specified time period (the
   336	    // `Ok(Some(_))` arm), then return the appropriate status code.
   337	    //
   338	    // If the process does not exit within that time (the `Ok(None)`
   339	    // arm) and `kill_after` is specified, then try sending `SIGKILL`.
   340	    //
   341	    // TODO The structure of this block is extremely similar to the
   342	    // structure of `wait_or_kill_process()`. They can probably be
   343	    // refactored into some common function.
   344	    match process.wait_or_timeout(duration) {
   345	        Ok(Some(status)) => Err(status
   346	            .code()
   347	            .unwrap_or_else(|| preserve_signal_info(status.signal().unwrap()))
   348	            .into()),
   349	        Ok(None) => {
   350	            report_if_verbose(signal, &cmd[0], verbose);
   351	            send_signal(process, signal, foreground);
   352	            match kill_after {
   353	                None => {
   354	                    let status = process.wait()?;
   355	                    if preserve_status {
   356	                        if let Some(ec) = status.code() {
   357	                            Err(ec.into())
   358	                        } else if let Some(sc) = status.signal() {
   359	                            Err(ExitStatus::SignalSent(sc.try_into().unwrap()).into())
   360	                        } else {
   361	                            Err(ExitStatus::CommandTimedOut.into())
   362	                        }
   363	                    } else {
   364	                        Err(ExitStatus::CommandTimedOut.into())
   365	                    }
   366	                }
   367	                Some(kill_after) => {
   368	                    match wait_or_kill_process(
   369	                        process,
   370	                        &cmd[0],
   371	                        kill_after,
   372	                        preserve_status,
   373	                        foreground,
   374	                        verbose,
   375	                    ) {
   376	                        Ok(status) => Err(status.into()),
   377	                        Err(e) => Err(USimpleError::new(
   378	                            ExitStatus::TimeoutFailed.into(),
   379	                            e.to_string(),
   380	                        )),
   381	                    }
   382	                }
   383	            }
   384	        }
   385	        Err(_) => {
   386	            // We're going to return ERR_EXIT_STATUS regardless of
   387	            // whether `send_signal()` succeeds or fails
   388	            send_signal(process, signal, foreground);
   389	            Err(ExitStatus::TimeoutFailed.into())
   390	        }
   391	    }
   392	}
   393

   299	
   300	/*
   301	   The following signals are defined in AIX:
   302	
   303	   SIGHUP     hangup, generated when terminal disconnects
   304	   SIGINT     interrupt, generated from terminal special char
   305	   SIGQUIT    quit, generated from terminal special char
   306	   SIGILL     illegal instruction (not reset when caught)
   307	   SIGTRAP    trace trap (not reset when caught)
   308	   SIGABRT    abort process
   309	   SIGEMT     EMT instruction
   310	   SIGFPE     floating point exception
   311	   SIGKILL    kill (cannot be caught or ignored)
   312	   SIGBUS     bus error (specification exception)
   313	   SIGSEGV    segmentation violation
   314	   SIGSYS     bad argument to system call
   315	   SIGPIPE    write on a pipe with no one to read it
   316	   SIGALRM    alarm clock timeout
   317	   SIGTERM    software termination signal
   318	   SIGURG     urgent condition on I/O channel
   319	   SIGSTOP    stop (cannot be caught or ignored)
   320	   SIGTSTP    interactive stop
   321	   SIGCONT    continue (cannot be caught or ignored)
   322	   SIGCHLD    sent to parent on child stop or exit
   323	   SIGTTIN    background read attempted from control terminal
   324	   SIGTTOU    background write attempted to control terminal
   325	   SIGIO      I/O possible, or completed
   326	   SIGXCPU    cpu time limit exceeded (see setrlimit())
   327	   SIGXFSZ    file size limit exceeded (see setrlimit())
   328	   SIGMSG     input data is in the ring buffer
   329	   SIGWINCH   window size changed
   330	   SIGPWR     power-fail restart
   331	   SIGUSR1    user defined signal 1
   332	   SIGUSR2    user defined signal 2
   333	   SIGPROF    profiling time alarm (see setitimer)
   334	   SIGDANGER  system crash imminent; free up some page space
   335	   SIGVTALRM  virtual time alarm (see setitimer)
   336	   SIGMIGRATE migrate process
   337	   SIGPRE     programming exception
   338	   SIGVIRT    AIX virtual time alarm
   339	   SIGTALRM   per-thread alarm clock
   340	*/
   341	#[cfg(target_os = "aix")]
   342	pub static ALL_SIGNALS: [&str; 37] = [
   343	    "HUP", "INT", "QUIT", "ILL", "TRAP", "ABRT", "EMT", "FPE", "KILL", "BUS", "SEGV", "SYS",
   344	    "PIPE", "ALRM", "TERM", "URG", "STOP", "TSTP", "CONT", "CHLD", "TTIN", "TTOU", "IO", "XCPU",
   345	    "XFSZ", "MSG", "WINCH", "PWR", "USR1", "USR2", "PROF", "DANGER", "VTALRM", "MIGRATE", "PRE",
   346	    "VIRT", "TALRM",
   347	];
   348	
   349	/// Returns the signal number for a given signal name or value.
   350	pub fn signal_by_name_or_value(signal_name_or_value: &str) -> Option<usize> {
   351	    let signal_name_upcase = signal_name_or_value.to_uppercase();
   352	    if let Ok(value) = signal_name_upcase.parse() {
   353	        return if is_signal(value) { Some(value) } else { None };
   354	    }
   355	    let signal_name = signal_name_upcase.trim_start_matches("SIG");
   356	
   357	    ALL_SIGNALS.iter().position(|&s| s == signal_name)
   358	}
   359	
   360	/// Returns true if the given number is a valid signal number.
   361	pub fn is_signal(num: usize) -> bool {
   362	    num < ALL_SIGNALS.len()
   363	}
   364	
   365	/// Returns the signal name for a given signal value.
   366	pub fn signal_name_by_value(signal_value: usize) -> Option<&'static str> {
   367	    ALL_SIGNALS.get(signal_value).copied()
   368	}
   369

    23	    unsafe { libc::geteuid() }

    51	
    52	/// `getsid()` returns the session ID of the process with process ID pid.
    53	///
    54	/// If pid is 0, getsid() returns the session ID of the calling process.
    55	///
    56	/// # Error
    57	///
    58	/// - [Errno::EPERM] A process with process ID pid exists, but it is not in the same session as the calling process, and the implementation considers this an error.
    59	/// - [Errno::ESRCH] No process with process ID pid was found.
    60	///
    61	///
    62	/// # Platform
    63	///
    64	/// This function only support standard POSIX implementation platform,
    65	/// so some system such as redox doesn't supported.
    66	#[cfg(not(target_os = "redox"))]
    67	pub fn getsid(pid: i32) -> Result<pid_t, Errno> {
    68	    unsafe {
    69	        let result = libc::getsid(pid);
    70	        if Errno::last() == Errno::UnknownErrno {
    71	            Ok(result)
    72	        } else {
    73	            Err(Errno::last())
    74	        }
    75	    }
    76	}
    77	
    78	/// Missing methods for Child objects
    79	pub trait ChildExt {
    80	    /// Send a signal to a Child process.
    81	    ///
    82	    /// Caller beware: if the process already exited then you may accidentally
    83	    /// send the signal to an unrelated process that recycled the PID.
    84	    fn send_signal(&mut self, signal: usize) -> io::Result<()>;
    85	
    86	    /// Send a signal to a process group.
    87	    fn send_signal_group(&mut self, signal: usize) -> io::Result<()>;
    88	
    89	    /// Wait for a process to finish or return after the specified duration.
    90	    /// A `timeout` of zero disables the timeout.
    91	    fn wait_or_timeout(&mut self, timeout: Duration) -> io::Result<Option<ExitStatus>>;
    92	}
    93	
    94	impl ChildExt for Child {
    95	    fn send_signal(&mut self, signal: usize) -> io::Result<()> {
    96	        if unsafe { libc::kill(self.id() as pid_t, signal as i32) } == 0 {
    97	            Ok(())
    98	        } else {
    99	            Err(io::Error::last_os_error())
   100	        }
   101	    }
   102	
   103	    fn send_signal_group(&mut self, signal: usize) -> io::Result<()> {
   104	        // Ignore the signal, so we don't go into a signal loop.
   105	        if unsafe { libc::signal(signal as i32, libc::SIG_IGN) } != 0 {
   106	            return Err(io::Error::last_os_error());
   107	        }
   108	        if unsafe { libc::kill(0, signal as i32) } == 0 {
   109	            Ok(())
   110	        } else {
   111	            Err(io::Error::last_os_error())
   112	        }
   113	    }
   114	
   115	    fn wait_or_timeout(&mut self, timeout: Duration) -> io::Result<Option<ExitStatus>> {
   116	        if timeout == Duration::from_micros(0) {
   117	            return self.wait().map(Some);
   118	        }
   119	        // .try_wait() doesn't drop stdin, so we do it manually
   120	        drop(self.stdin.take());
   121	
   122	        let start = Instant::now();
   123	        loop {
   124	            if let Some(status) = self.try_wait()? {
   125	                return Ok(Some(status));
   126	            }
   127	
   128	            if start.elapsed() >= timeout {
   129	                break;
   130	            }
   131	
   132	            // XXX: this is kinda gross, but it's cleaner than starting a thread just to wait
   133	            //      (which was the previous solution).  We might want to use a different duration
   134	            //      here as well
   135	            thread::sleep(Duration::from_millis(100));
   136	        }
   137	
   138	        Ok(None)
   139	    }
   140	}

   144	    use super::*;

   146	    #[test]
   147	    #[cfg(not(target_os = "redox"))]
   148	    fn test_getsid() {
   149	        assert_eq!(
   150	            getsid(getpid()).expect("getsid(getpid)"),
   151	            // zero is a special value for SID.
   152	            // https://pubs.opengroup.org/onlinepubs/9699919799/functions/getsid.html
   153	            getsid(0).expect("getsid(0)")
   154	        );
   155	
   156	        // SID never be 0.
   157	        assert!(getsid(getpid()).expect("getsid(getpid)") > 0);
   158	
   159	        // This might caused tests failure but the probability is low.
   160	        assert!(getsid(999_999).is_err());
   161	    }

set -e

echo "Building timeout..."
cd /testbed
cargo build --bin timeout 2>&1 | tail -5

echo ""
echo "Testing GNU timeout behavior (reference)..."
# Test if GNU timeout is available
if command -v /usr/bin/timeout &> /dev/null; then
    echo "Starting GNU timeout with sleep 42..."
    /usr/bin/timeout 42 sleep 42 &
    TIMEOUT_PID=$!
    sleep 0.5  # Give it time to start
    
    # Find the child sleep process
    SLEEP_PID=$(pgrep -P $TIMEOUT_PID sleep || echo "")
    
    if [ -n "$SLEEP_PID" ]; then
        echo "Timeout PID: $TIMEOUT_PID, Sleep PID: $SLEEP_PID"
        echo "Sending TERM signal to timeout..."
        kill -TERM $TIMEOUT_PID
        sleep 0.5
        
        # Check if sleep is still running
        if ps -p $SLEEP_PID > /dev/null 2>&1; then
            echo "❌ GNU timeout: Sleep process is still running!"
            kill -9 $SLEEP_PID 2>/dev/null || true
        else
            echo "✓ GNU timeout: Sleep process was terminated correctly"
        fi
    else
        echo "Could not find child sleep process"
    fi
    
    # Cleanup
    kill -9 $TIMEOUT_PID 2>/dev/null || true
fi

echo ""
echo "Testing uutils timeout behavior..."
cd /testbed
echo "Starting uutils timeout with sleep 42..."
./target/debug/timeout 42 sleep 42 &
TIMEOUT_PID=$!
sleep 0.5  # Give it time to start

# Find the child sleep process
SLEEP_PID=$(pgrep -P $TIMEOUT_PID sleep || echo "")

if [ -n "$SLEEP_PID" ]; then
    echo "Timeout PID: $TIMEOUT_PID, Sleep PID: $SLEEP_PID"
    echo "Sending TERM signal to timeout..."
    kill -TERM $TIMEOUT_PID
    sleep 0.5
    
    # Check if sleep is still running
    if ps -p $SLEEP_PID > /dev/null 2>&1; then
        echo "❌ UUTILS timeout: Sleep process is still running (BUG CONFIRMED!)"
        # Check who the parent is now
        PPID=$(ps -o ppid= -p $SLEEP_PID | tr -d '"'"' '"'"')
        echo "   Sleep process parent PID is now: $PPID"
        kill -9 $SLEEP_PID 2>/dev/null || true
    else
        echo "✓ UUTILS timeout: Sleep process was terminated correctly"
    fi
else
    echo "Could not find child sleep process"
fi

# Cleanup
kill -9 $TIMEOUT_PID 2>/dev/null || true

echo ""
echo "Test complete!"

str_replace_editor create /testbed/test_simple.sh --file_text '#!/bin/bash

echo "Testing GNU timeout behavior (reference)..."
# Test if GNU timeout is available
if command -v /usr/bin/timeout &> /dev/null; then
    echo "Starting GNU timeout with sleep 42..."
    /usr/bin/timeout 42 sleep 42 &
    TIMEOUT_PID=$!
    sleep 0.5  # Give it time to start
    
    # Find the child sleep process
    SLEEP_PID=$(pgrep -P $TIMEOUT_PID sleep || echo "")
    
    if [ -n "$SLEEP_PID" ]; then
        echo "Timeout PID: $TIMEOUT_PID, Sleep PID: $SLEEP_PID"
        echo "Sending TERM signal to timeout..."
        kill -TERM $TIMEOUT_PID
        sleep 0.5
        
        # Check if sleep is still running
        if ps -p $SLEEP_PID > /dev/null 2>&1; then
            echo "❌ GNU timeout: Sleep process is still running!"
            kill -9 $SLEEP_PID 2>/dev/null || true
        else
            echo "✓ GNU timeout: Sleep process was terminated correctly"
        fi
    else
        echo "Could not find child sleep process"
    fi
    
    # Cleanup
    kill -9 $TIMEOUT_PID 2>/dev/null || true
fi

echo ""
echo "Testing uutils timeout behavior..."
cd /testbed
echo "Starting uutils timeout with sleep 42..."
./target/debug/coreutils timeout 42 sleep 42 &
TIMEOUT_PID=$!
sleep 0.5  # Give it time to start

# Find the child sleep process
SLEEP_PID=$(pgrep -P $TIMEOUT_PID sleep || echo "")

if [ -n "$SLEEP_PID" ]; then
    echo "Timeout PID: $TIMEOUT_PID, Sleep PID: $SLEEP_PID"
    echo "Sending TERM signal to timeout..."
    kill -TERM $TIMEOUT_PID
    sleep 0.5
    
    # Check if sleep is still running
    if ps -p $SLEEP_PID > /dev/null 2>&1; then
        echo "❌ UUTILS timeout: Sleep process is still running (BUG CONFIRMED!)"
        # Check who the parent is now
        PPID=$(ps -o ppid= -p $SLEEP_PID | tr -d '"'"' '"'"')
        echo "   Sleep process parent PID is now: $PPID"
        kill -9 $SLEEP_PID 2>/dev/null || true
    else
        echo "✓ UUTILS timeout: Sleep process was terminated correctly"
    fi
else
    echo "Could not find child sleep process"
fi

# Cleanup
kill -9 $TIMEOUT_PID 2>/dev/null || true

echo ""
echo "Test complete!"

Perfect! I've confirmed the bug. The uutils timeout doesn't terminate the child process when it receives a TERM signal. Now let me analyze the code to understand the issue.

Looking at the timeout.rs code, I can see that:

1. The timeout command spawns a child process
2. It waits for the duration and sends signals if needed
3. However, there's no signal handler set up to catch TERM/INT signals sent to the timeout process itself

Let me look at the GNU coreutils timeout source code online reference and understand the expected behavior. The key issue is that when timeout receives a signal (like TERM), it should:

1. Forward the signal to the child process (or process group)
2. Then exit

Let me create a fix. I need to:
1. Set up signal handlers for common termination signals (TERM, INT, HUP, etc.)

3. Then exit appropriately

use signal_hook::iterator::Handle;
use uucore::{
    error::UResult,
    format::num_format::{FloatVariant, Formatter},
};

use crate::numbers::{SuffixType, to_magnitude_and_suffix};

#[derive(PartialEq, Eq)]
pub(crate) enum ProgUpdateType {
    Periodic,
    Signal,
    Final,
}

/// Summary statistics for read and write progress of dd for a given duration.
pub(crate) struct ProgUpdate {
    /// Read statistics.
    ///
    /// This contains information about the number of blocks read from
    /// the data source.
    pub(crate) read_stat: ReadStat,

    /// Write statistics.
    ///
    /// This contains information about the number of blocks and
    /// number of bytes written to the data sink.
    pub(crate) write_stat: WriteStat,

    /// The time period over which the reads and writes were measured.
    pub(crate) duration: Duration,
--
        use signal_hook::consts::signal::*;
        use signal_hook::iterator::Signals;

        let mut signals = Signals::new([SIGUSR1])?;
        let handle = signals.handle();
        let thread = std::thread::spawn(move || {
            for signal in &mut signals {
                match signal {
                    SIGUSR1 => (*f)(),
                    _ => unreachable!(),
                }
            }
        });

        Ok(Self {
            handle,
            thread: Some(thread),
        })
    }
}

#[cfg(target_os = "linux")]
impl Drop for SignalHandler {
    fn drop(&mut self) {
        self.handle.close();
        if let Some(thread) = std::mem::take(&mut self.thread) {
            thread.join().unwrap();
        }
    }
}

I see how signal_hook works. However, for timeout, I think a simpler approach might work better. Let me think about the problem:

1. When timeout receives a signal (like TERM), it should forward it to the child and exit
2. We need to handle this gracefully

Looking at the GNU timeout source, I found that it uses signal handlers to catch termination signals and forward them to the child process. The key is that we need to:

1. Set up signal handlers before waiting for the child
2. When a signal is received, send it to the child process (or process group)
3. Then terminate

Let me look at a different approach. Instead of using signal_hook which requires spawning a thread, I can use nix's sigaction to set up signal handlers. But actually, there's a simpler solution - we can use a shared atomic variable with signal_hook to check if a signal was received during the wait loop.

Let me implement the fix:

   115	    fn wait_or_timeout(&mut self, timeout: Duration) -> io::Result<Option<ExitStatus>> {
   116	        if timeout == Duration::from_micros(0) {
   117	            return self.wait().map(Some);
   118	        }
   119	        // .try_wait() doesn't drop stdin, so we do it manually
   120	        drop(self.stdin.take());
   121	
   122	        let start = Instant::now();
   123	        loop {
   124	            if let Some(status) = self.try_wait()? {
   125	                return Ok(Some(status));
   126	            }
   127	
   128	            if start.elapsed() >= timeout {
   129	                break;
   130	            }
   131	
   132	            // XXX: this is kinda gross, but it's cleaner than starting a thread just to wait
   133	            //      (which was the previous solution).  We might want to use a different duration
   134	            //      here as well
   135	            thread::sleep(Duration::from_millis(100));
   136	        }
   137	
   138	        Ok(None)
   139	    }

   296	/// TODO: Improve exit codes, and make them consistent with the GNU Coreutils exit codes.
   297	fn timeout(
   298	    cmd: &[String],
   299	    duration: Duration,
   300	    signal: usize,
   301	    kill_after: Option<Duration>,
   302	    foreground: bool,
   303	    preserve_status: bool,
   304	    verbose: bool,
   305	) -> UResult<()> {
   306	    if !foreground {
   307	        unsafe { libc::setpgid(0, 0) };
   308	    }
   309	    #[cfg(unix)]
   310	    enable_pipe_errors()?;
   311	
   312	    let process = &mut process::Command::new(&cmd[0])
   313	        .args(&cmd[1..])
   314	        .stdin(Stdio::inherit())
   315	        .stdout(Stdio::inherit())
   316	        .stderr(Stdio::inherit())
   317	        .spawn()
   318	        .map_err(|err| {
   319	            let status_code = if err.kind() == ErrorKind::NotFound {
   320	                // FIXME: not sure which to use
   321	                127
   322	            } else {
   323	                // FIXME: this may not be 100% correct...
   324	                126
   325	            };
   326	            USimpleError::new(
   327	                status_code,
   328	                get_message_with_args(
   329	                    "timeout-error-failed-to-execute-process",
   330	                    HashMap::from([("error".to_string(), err.to_string())]),
   331	                ),
   332	            )
   333	        })?;
   334	    unblock_sigchld();
   335	    // Wait for the child process for the specified time period.
   336	    //
   337	    // If the process exits within the specified time period (the
   338	    // `Ok(Some(_))` arm), then return the appropriate status code.
   339	    //
   340	    // If the process does not exit within that time (the `Ok(None)`
   341	    // arm) and `kill_after` is specified, then try sending `SIGKILL`.
   342	    //
   343	    // TODO The structure of this block is extremely similar to the
   344	    // structure of `wait_or_kill_process()`. They can probably be
   345	    // refactored into some common function.

   347	        Ok(Some(status)) => Err(status
   348	            .code()
   349	            .unwrap_or_else(|| preserve_signal_info(status.signal().unwrap()))
   350	            .into()),
   351	        Ok(None) => {
   352	            report_if_verbose(signal, &cmd[0], verbose);
   353	            send_signal(process, signal, foreground);
   354	            match kill_after {
   355	                None => {
   356	                    let status = process.wait()?;
   357	                    if preserve_status {
   358	                        if let Some(ec) = status.code() {
   359	                            Err(ec.into())
   360	                        } else if let Some(sc) = status.signal() {
   361	                            Err(ExitStatus::SignalSent(sc.try_into().unwrap()).into())
   362	                        } else {
   363	                            Err(ExitStatus::CommandTimedOut.into())
   364	                        }
   365	                    } else {
   366	                        Err(ExitStatus::CommandTimedOut.into())
   367	                    }
   368	                }
   369	                Some(kill_after) => {
   370	                    match wait_or_kill_process(
   371	                        process,
   372	                        &cmd[0],
   373	                        kill_after,
   374	                        preserve_status,
   375	                        foreground,
   376	                        verbose,
   377	                    ) {
   378	                        Ok(status) => Err(status.into()),
   379	                        Err(e) => Err(USimpleError::new(
   380	                            ExitStatus::TimeoutFailed.into(),
   381	                            e.to_string(),
   382	                        )),
   383	                    }
   384	                }
   385	            }
   386	        }
   387	        Err(_) => {
   388	            // We're going to return ERR_EXIT_STATUS regardless of
   389	            // whether `send_signal()` succeeds or fails
   390	            send_signal(process, signal, foreground);
   391	            Err(ExitStatus::TimeoutFailed.into())
   392	        }

fn unblock_sigchld() {
    unsafe {
        nix::sys::signal::signal(
            nix::sys::signal::Signal::SIGCHLD,
            nix::sys::signal::SigHandler::SigDfl,
        )
        .unwrap();
    }
}

/// Set up signal handlers to forward termination signals to the child process.
///
/// Returns an Arc<AtomicBool> that will be set to true when a termination signal is received.
fn setup_signal_handlers() -> std::io::Result<Arc<AtomicBool>> {
    use signal_hook::consts::signal::*;
    use signal_hook::flag;

    let term_now = Arc::new(AtomicBool::new(false));
    
    // Register handlers for common termination signals
    // These are the signals that should cause timeout to forward the signal to the child and exit
    for sig in &[SIGTERM, SIGINT, SIGHUP, SIGQUIT] {
        flag::register(*sig, Arc::clone(&term_now))?;
    }
    
    Ok(term_now)
}

/// Wait for a child process with support for signal interruption.
///
/// This function is similar to `wait_or_timeout` but also checks for termination signals.
/// If a termination signal is received, it returns Ok(None) to indicate timeout/interruption.
fn wait_or_timeout_with_signal_check(
    process: &mut Child,
    duration: Duration,
    term_signal: &Arc<AtomicBool>,
) -> std::io::Result<Option<std::process::ExitStatus>> {
    use std::thread;
    use std::time::Instant;

    if duration == Duration::from_micros(0) {
        return process.wait().map(Some);
    }
    
    // .try_wait() doesn'"'"'t drop stdin, so we do it manually
    drop(process.stdin.take());

    let start = Instant::now();
    loop {
        // Check if we received a termination signal
        if term_signal.load(Ordering::Relaxed) {
            return Ok(None);
        }

        if let Some(status) = process.try_wait()? {
            return Ok(Some(status));
        }

        if start.elapsed() >= duration {
            break;
        }

        // Sleep for a short period before checking again
        thread::sleep(Duration::from_millis(100));
    }

    Ok(None)
}'

str_replace_editor str_replace /testbed/src/uu/timeout/src/timeout.rs   --old_str '/// TODO: Improve exit codes, and make them consistent with the GNU Coreutils exit codes.
fn timeout(
    cmd: &[String],
    duration: Duration,
    signal: usize,
    kill_after: Option<Duration>,
    foreground: bool,
    preserve_status: bool,
    verbose: bool,
) -> UResult<()> {
    if !foreground {
        unsafe { libc::setpgid(0, 0) };
    }
    #[cfg(unix)]
    enable_pipe_errors()?;

    let process = &mut process::Command::new(&cmd[0])
        .args(&cmd[1..])
        .stdin(Stdio::inherit())
        .stdout(Stdio::inherit())
        .stderr(Stdio::inherit())
        .spawn()
        .map_err(|err| {
            let status_code = if err.kind() == ErrorKind::NotFound {
                // FIXME: not sure which to use
                127
            } else {
                // FIXME: this may not be 100% correct...
                126
            };
            USimpleError::new(
                status_code,
                get_message_with_args(
                    "timeout-error-failed-to-execute-process",
                    HashMap::from([("error".to_string(), err.to_string())]),
                ),
            )
        })?;
    unblock_sigchld();
    // Wait for the child process for the specified time period.
    //
    // If the process exits within the specified time period (the
    // `Ok(Some(_))` arm), then return the appropriate status code.
    //
    // If the process does not exit within that time (the `Ok(None)`
    // arm) and `kill_after` is specified, then try sending `SIGKILL`.
    //
    // TODO The structure of this block is extremely similar to the
    // structure of `wait_or_kill_process()`. They can probably be
    // refactored into some common function.
    match process.wait_or_timeout(duration) {
        Ok(Some(status)) => Err(status
            .code()
            .unwrap_or_else(|| preserve_signal_info(status.signal().unwrap()))
            .into()),
        Ok(None) => {
            report_if_verbose(signal, &cmd[0], verbose);
            send_signal(process, signal, foreground);
            match kill_after {
                None => {
                    let status = process.wait()?;
                    if preserve_status {
                        if let Some(ec) = status.code() {
                            Err(ec.into())
                        } else if let Some(sc) = status.signal() {
                            Err(ExitStatus::SignalSent(sc.try_into().unwrap()).into())
                        } else {
                            Err(ExitStatus::CommandTimedOut.into())
                        }
                    } else {
                        Err(ExitStatus::CommandTimedOut.into())
                    }
                }
                Some(kill_after) => {
                    match wait_or_kill_process(
                        process,
                        &cmd[0],
                        kill_after,
                        preserve_status,
                        foreground,
                        verbose,
                    ) {
                        Ok(status) => Err(status.into()),
                        Err(e) => Err(USimpleError::new(
                            ExitStatus::TimeoutFailed.into(),
                            e.to_string(),
                        )),
                    }
                }
            }
        }
        Err(_) => {
            // We'"'"'re going to return ERR_EXIT_STATUS regardless of
            // whether `send_signal()` succeeds or fails
            send_signal(process, signal, foreground);
            Err(ExitStatus::TimeoutFailed.into())
        }
    }
}' --new_str '/// TODO: Improve exit codes, and make them consistent with the GNU Coreutils exit codes.
fn timeout(
    cmd: &[String],
    duration: Duration,
    signal: usize,
    kill_after: Option<Duration>,
    foreground: bool,
    preserve_status: bool,
    verbose: bool,
) -> UResult<()> {
    if !foreground {
        unsafe { libc::setpgid(0, 0) };
    }
    #[cfg(unix)]
    enable_pipe_errors()?;

    let process = &mut process::Command::new(&cmd[0])
        .args(&cmd[1..])
        .stdin(Stdio::inherit())
        .stdout(Stdio::inherit())
        .stderr(Stdio::inherit())
        .spawn()
        .map_err(|err| {
            let status_code = if err.kind() == ErrorKind::NotFound {
                // FIXME: not sure which to use
                127
            } else {
                // FIXME: this may not be 100% correct...
                126
            };
            USimpleError::new(
                status_code,
                get_message_with_args(
                    "timeout-error-failed-to-execute-process",
                    HashMap::from([("error".to_string(), err.to_string())]),
                ),
            )
        })?;
    unblock_sigchld();
    
    // Set up signal handlers to catch termination signals
    let term_signal = setup_signal_handlers()
        .map_err(|e| USimpleError::new(ExitStatus::TimeoutFailed.into(), e.to_string()))?;
    
    // Wait for the child process for the specified time period.
    //
    // If the process exits within the specified time period (the
    // `Ok(Some(_))` arm), then return the appropriate status code.
    //
    // If the process does not exit within that time (the `Ok(None)`
    // arm) and `kill_after` is specified, then try sending `SIGKILL`.
    //
    // TODO The structure of this block is extremely similar to the
    // structure of `wait_or_kill_process()`. They can probably be
    // refactored into some common function.
    match wait_or_timeout_with_signal_check(process, duration, &term_signal) {
        Ok(Some(status)) => Err(status
            .code()
            .unwrap_or_else(|| preserve_signal_info(status.signal().unwrap()))
            .into()),
        Ok(None) => {
            // Check if we'"'"'re here because of a signal or timeout
            let interrupted = term_signal.load(Ordering::Relaxed);
            
            // Send the configured signal to the child
            report_if_verbose(signal, &cmd[0], verbose);
            send_signal(process, signal, foreground);
            
            // If we were interrupted by a signal, we should exit immediately
            // matching GNU timeout'"'"'s behavior
            if interrupted {
                // Wait a short time for the child to exit
                let _ = process.wait();
                // Exit with status indicating termination by signal
                // GNU timeout exits with 124 + signal number when terminated by signal
                std::process::exit(128 + signal as i32);
            }
            
            match kill_after {
                None => {
                    let status = process.wait()?;
                    if preserve_status {
                        if let Some(ec) = status.code() {
                            Err(ec.into())
                        } else if let Some(sc) = status.signal() {
                            Err(ExitStatus::SignalSent(sc.try_into().unwrap()).into())
                        } else {
                            Err(ExitStatus::CommandTimedOut.into())
                        }
                    } else {
                        Err(ExitStatus::CommandTimedOut.into())
                    }
                }
                Some(kill_after) => {
                    match wait_or_kill_process(
                        process,
                        &cmd[0],
                        kill_after,
                        preserve_status,
                        foreground,
                        verbose,
                    ) {
                        Ok(status) => Err(status.into()),
                        Err(e) => Err(USimpleError::new(
                            ExitStatus::TimeoutFailed.into(),
                            e.to_string(),
                        )),
                    }
                }
            }
        }
        Err(_) => {
            // We'"'"'re going to return ERR_EXIT_STATUS regardless of
            // whether `send_signal()` succeeds or fails
            send_signal(process, signal, foreground);
            Err(ExitStatus::TimeoutFailed.into())
        }
    }
}'

I see the issue - the timeout process is still running after receiving TERM. That means the signal handler is not working as expected. Let me check if there's an issue with how signals are being handled. The problem might be that signal_hook::flag is not the right approach when there's a process group involved.

1. Forward the signal to the child (or process group)
2. Exit

The issue is that we're using `flag::register` which just sets a flag, but we're still in the wait loop. We need to actually handle the signal more actively. Let me look at a different approach using sigaction or signal handlers that will actually interrupt the wait.

Actually, I think the issue is simpler - when we receive a signal in the parent process (timeout), the child doesn't automatically receive it. We need to explicitly forward it. But the problem is that after we forward it, the timeout process itself still needs to exit properly.

Let me re-think this. Looking at the GNU source code conceptually:
1. It sets up signal handlers for TERM, INT, HUP, etc.
2. When a signal is received, it forwards it to the child process
3. Then it waits for the child or kills it
4. Then exits

The key issue is that my current implementation only checks the flag during the wait loop, but doesn't actually interrupt the parent process when the signal arrives. Let me try a different approach - I'll use signal-hook to directly exit after forwarding the signal:

🎬 ACTION
str_replace_editor str_replace /testbed/src/uu/timeout/src/timeout.rs   --old_str '/// Set up signal handlers to forward termination signals to the child process.
///
/// Returns an Arc<AtomicBool> that will be set to true when a termination signal is received.
fn setup_signal_handlers() -> std::io::Result<Arc<AtomicBool>> {
    use signal_hook::consts::signal::*;
    use signal_hook::flag;

    let term_now = Arc::new(AtomicBool::new(false));
    
    // Register handlers for common termination signals
    // These are the signals that should cause timeout to forward the signal to the child and exit
    for sig in &[SIGTERM, SIGINT, SIGHUP, SIGQUIT] {
        flag::register(*sig, Arc::clone(&term_now))?;
    }
    
    Ok(term_now)
}' --new_str '/// Set up signal handlers to forward termination signals to the child process.
///
/// This function sets up handlers that will send signals to the child process
/// and then exit when the timeout process receives termination signals.
fn setup_signal_handlers(child_pid: i32, foreground: bool) -> std::io::Result<()> {
    use signal_hook::consts::signal::*;
    use signal_hook::iterator::Signals;
    
    // Create a signal set for the signals we want to catch
    let mut signals = Signals::new(&[SIGTERM, SIGINT, SIGHUP, SIGQUIT])?;
    
    // Spawn a thread to handle signals
    std::thread::spawn(move || {
        for sig in signals.forever() {
            // Forward the signal to the child process or process group
            if foreground {
                unsafe {
                    libc::kill(child_pid, sig);
                }
            } else {
                // Send to the entire process group
                unsafe {
                    libc::kill(0, sig);
                }
            }
            // Exit immediately after forwarding the signal
            // This matches GNU timeout behavior
            process::exit(128 + sig);
        }
    });
    
    Ok(())
}'

   190	/// Set up signal handlers to forward termination signals to the child process.
   191	///
   192	/// This function sets up handlers that will send signals to the child process
   193	/// and then exit when the timeout process receives termination signals.
   194	fn setup_signal_handlers(child_pid: i32, foreground: bool) -> std::io::Result<()> {
   195	    use signal_hook::consts::signal::*;
   196	    use signal_hook::iterator::Signals;
   197	    
   198	    // Create a signal set for the signals we want to catch
   199	    let mut signals = Signals::new(&[SIGTERM, SIGINT, SIGHUP, SIGQUIT])?;
   200	    
   201	    // Spawn a thread to handle signals
   202	    std::thread::spawn(move || {
   203	        for sig in signals.forever() {
   204	            // Forward the signal to the child process or process group
   205	            if foreground {
   206	                unsafe {
   207	                    libc::kill(child_pid, sig);
   208	                }
   209	            } else {
   210	                // Send to the entire process group
   211	                unsafe {
   212	                    libc::kill(0, sig);
   213	                }
   214	            }
   215	            // Exit immediately after forwarding the signal
   216	            // This matches GNU timeout behavior
   217	            process::exit(128 + sig);
   218	        }
   219	    });
   220	    
   221	    Ok(())
   222	}

str_replace_editor str_replace /testbed/src/uu/timeout/src/timeout.rs   --old_str '/// Wait for a child process with support for signal interruption.
///
/// This function is similar to `wait_or_timeout` but also checks for termination signals.
/// If a termination signal is received, it returns Ok(None) to indicate timeout/interruption.
fn wait_or_timeout_with_signal_check(
    process: &mut Child,
    duration: Duration,
    term_signal: &Arc<AtomicBool>,
) -> std::io::Result<Option<process::ExitStatus>> {
    use std::thread;
    use std::time::Instant;

    if duration == Duration::from_micros(0) {
        return process.wait().map(Some);
    }
    
    // .try_wait() doesn'"'"'t drop stdin, so we do it manually
    drop(process.stdin.take());

    let start = Instant::now();
    loop {
        // Check if we received a termination signal
        if term_signal.load(Ordering::Relaxed) {
            return Ok(None);
        }

        if let Some(status) = process.try_wait()? {
            return Ok(Some(status));
        }

        if start.elapsed() >= duration {
            break;
        }

        // Sleep for a short period before checking again
        thread::sleep(Duration::from_millis(100));
    }

    Ok(None)
}' --new_str ''

cat > /tmp/test_edge_cases.sh << 'EOF'
#!/bin/bash

echo "Test 1: Normal timeout expiration (should work as before)"
timeout 0.5 sleep 10
EXIT_CODE=$?
if [ $EXIT_CODE -eq 124 ]; then
    echo "✓ Test 1 passed: Exit code is 124 for timeout"
else
    echo "✗ Test 1 failed: Exit code is $EXIT_CODE instead of 124"
fi

echo ""
echo "Test 2: Command completes before timeout"
timeout 5 sleep 0.1
EXIT_CODE=$?
if [ $EXIT_CODE -eq 0 ]; then
    echo "✓ Test 2 passed: Exit code is 0 for successful completion"
else
    echo "✗ Test 2 failed: Exit code is $EXIT_CODE instead of 0"
fi

echo ""
echo "Test 3: Sending INT signal to timeout"
timeout 42 sleep 42 &
PID=$!
sleep 0.5
SLEEP_PID=$(pgrep -P $PID sleep || echo "")
if [ -n "$SLEEP_PID" ]; then
    kill -INT $PID
    sleep 0.5
    if ps -p $SLEEP_PID > /dev/null 2>&1; then
        echo "✗ Test 3 failed: Sleep is still running after INT"
        kill -9 $SLEEP_PID 2>/dev/null
    else
        echo "✓ Test 3 passed: Sleep was terminated after INT"
    fi
else
    echo "✗ Test 3 failed: Could not find sleep process"
fi

echo ""
echo "Test 4: Sending HUP signal to timeout"
timeout 42 sleep 42 &
PID=$!
sleep 0.5
SLEEP_PID=$(pgrep -P $PID sleep || echo "")
if [ -n "$SLEEP_PID" ]; then
    kill -HUP $PID
    sleep 0.5
    if ps -p $SLEEP_PID > /dev/null 2>&1; then
        echo "✗ Test 4 failed: Sleep is still running after HUP"
        kill -9 $SLEEP_PID 2>/dev/null
    else
        echo "✓ Test 4 passed: Sleep was terminated after HUP"
    fi
else
    echo "✗ Test 4 failed: Could not find sleep process"
fi

echo ""
echo "Test 5: With foreground mode"
timeout --foreground 42 sleep 42 &
PID=$!
sleep 0.5
SLEEP_PID=$(pgrep -P $PID sleep || echo "")
if [ -n "$SLEEP_PID" ]; then
    kill -TERM $PID
    sleep 0.5
    if ps -p $SLEEP_PID > /dev/null 2>&1; then
        echo "✗ Test 5 failed: Sleep is still running after TERM in foreground mode"
        kill -9 $SLEEP_PID 2>/dev/null
    else
        echo "✓ Test 5 passed: Sleep was terminated after TERM in foreground mode"
    fi
else
    echo "✗ Test 5 failed: Could not find sleep process"
fi

echo ""
echo "All tests completed!"
EOF
chmod +x /tmp/test_edge_cases.sh
cd /testbed && /tmp/test_edge_cases.sh

cat > /tmp/test_kill_after.sh << 'EOF'
#!/bin/bash

echo "Test: timeout with kill-after option"

# Create a script that ignores TERM signal
cat > /tmp/ignore_term.sh << 'INNER_EOF'
#!/bin/bash
trap '' TERM
sleep 100
INNER_EOF
chmod +x /tmp/ignore_term.sh

# Test that kill-after actually kills the process
timeout --kill-after=0.5 1 /tmp/ignore_term.sh &
PID=$!
sleep 2

# Check if the process is gone
if ps -p $PID > /dev/null 2>&1; then
    echo "✗ Test failed: timeout is still running"
    kill -9 $PID 2>/dev/null
else
    echo "✓ Test passed: Process was killed after grace period"
fi

# Cleanup
rm -f /tmp/ignore_term.sh

echo ""
echo "Test: Sending signal to timeout with kill-after"
timeout --kill-after=0.5 42 sleep 42 &
PID=$!
sleep 0.5
SLEEP_PID=$(pgrep -P $PID sleep || echo "")
if [ -n "$SLEEP_PID" ]; then
    kill -TERM $PID
    sleep 1
    if ps -p $SLEEP_PID > /dev/null 2>&1; then
        echo "✗ Test failed: Sleep is still running"
        kill -9 $SLEEP_PID 2>/dev/null
    else
        echo "✓ Test passed: Sleep was terminated correctly with kill-after"
    fi
else
    echo "✗ Test failed: Could not find sleep process"
fi

echo ""
echo "Kill-after tests completed!"
EOF
chmod +x /tmp/test_kill_after.sh
cd /testbed && /tmp/test_kill_after.sh

cat > /tmp/test_pr_scenario.sh << 'EOF'
#!/bin/bash

echo "=== Testing PR Scenario: timeout terminating child process on TERM signal ==="
echo ""

# Test 1: Basic TERM signal handling
echo "Test 1: Basic TERM signal handling"
/testbed/target/debug/timeout 42 sleep 42 &
TIMEOUT_PID=$!
sleep 0.5

# Find the child sleep process
SLEEP_PID=$(pgrep -P $TIMEOUT_PID sleep || echo "")

if [ -z "$SLEEP_PID" ]; then
    echo "✗ Could not find child sleep process"
    kill -9 $TIMEOUT_PID 2>/dev/null
    exit 1
fi

echo "  Timeout PID: $TIMEOUT_PID, Sleep PID: $SLEEP_PID"
echo "  Sending TERM signal to timeout..."
kill -TERM $TIMEOUT_PID
sleep 1

# Check if sleep is still running
if ps -p $SLEEP_PID > /dev/null 2>&1; then
    echo "✗ Test 1 FAILED: Sleep process is still running!"
    echo "  Sleep process parent PID is now: $(ps -o ppid= -p $SLEEP_PID | tr -d ' ')"
    kill -9 $SLEEP_PID 2>/dev/null
    TEST1_RESULT="FAILED"
else
    echo "✓ Test 1 PASSED: Sleep process was terminated correctly"
    TEST1_RESULT="PASSED"
fi

# Cleanup
kill -9 $TIMEOUT_PID 2>/dev/null || true

echo ""
echo "Test 2: Multiple concurrent timeout processes"
echo "  Starting 5 timeout processes..."

PIDS=()
for i in {1..5}; do
    /testbed/target/debug/timeout 42 sleep 42 &
    PIDS+=($!)
done

sleep 0.5

echo "  Terminating all timeout processes..."
for pid in "${PIDS[@]}"; do
    kill -TERM $pid 2>/dev/null
done

sleep 1

# Check if any sleep processes are still running
ORPHAN_COUNT=$(pgrep -f "sleep 42" | wc -l)

if [ $ORPHAN_COUNT -gt 0 ]; then
    echo "✗ Test 2 FAILED: $ORPHAN_COUNT orphaned sleep processes found!"
    pkill -9 -f "sleep 42"
    TEST2_RESULT="FAILED"
else
    echo "✓ Test 2 PASSED: No orphaned sleep processes"
    TEST2_RESULT="PASSED"
fi

# Cleanup any remaining processes
for pid in "${PIDS[@]}"; do
    kill -9 $pid 2>/dev/null || true
done

echo ""
echo "Test 3: Cleanup simulating the tail/inotify scenario from PR"
echo "  This simulates running timeout in tests where TERM signal is used for cleanup"

# Simulate test scenario: start multiple timeout commands and then cleanup
for i in {1..3}; do
    /testbed/target/debug/timeout 10 tail -f /dev/null &
    echo "  Started timeout+tail process (PID: $!)"
    sleep 0.2
done

sleep 0.5

echo "  Sending TERM to all timeout processes (simulating test cleanup)..."
pkill -TERM -f "^/testbed/target/debug/timeout"
sleep 1

# Check if any tail processes are orphaned
TAIL_COUNT=$(pgrep -f "tail -f /dev/null" | wc -l)

if [ $TAIL_COUNT -gt 0 ]; then
    echo "✗ Test 3 FAILED: $TAIL_COUNT orphaned tail processes found!"
    pkill -9 -f "tail -f /dev/null"
    TEST3_RESULT="FAILED"
else
    echo "✓ Test 3 PASSED: No orphaned tail processes"
    TEST3_RESULT="PASSED"
fi

# Final cleanup
pkill -9 -f "^/testbed/target/debug/timeout" 2>/dev/null || true
pkill -9 -f "tail -f /dev/null" 2>/dev/null || true

echo ""
echo "=== Test Results ==="
echo "Test 1 (Basic TERM handling): $TEST1_RESULT"
echo "Test 2 (Multiple processes): $TEST2_RESULT"
echo "Test 3 (tail/inotify scenario): $TEST3_RESULT"

if [ "$TEST1_RESULT" = "PASSED" ] && [ "$TEST2_RESULT" = "PASSED" ] && [ "$TEST3_RESULT" = "PASSED" ]; then
    echo ""
    echo "✓ ALL TESTS PASSED - PR issue is fixed!"
    exit 0
else
    echo ""
    echo "✗ SOME TESTS FAILED - PR issue not fully resolved"
    exit 1
fi
EOF

   191	/// and then exit when the timeout process receives termination signals.
   192	fn setup_signal_handlers(child_pid: i32, foreground: bool) -> std::io::Result<()> {
   193	    use signal_hook::consts::signal::*;
   194	    use signal_hook::iterator::Signals;
   195	    
   196	    // Create a signal set for the signals we want to catch
   197	    let mut signals = Signals::new(&[SIGTERM, SIGINT, SIGHUP, SIGQUIT])?;
   198	    
   199	    // Spawn a thread to handle signals
   200	    std::thread::spawn(move || {
   201	        for sig in signals.forever() {
   202	            // Forward the signal to the child process or process group
   203	            if foreground {
   204	                unsafe {
   205	                    libc::kill(child_pid, sig);
   206	                }

   208	                // Send to the entire process group

   211	                }
   212	            }

   214	            // This matches GNU timeout behavior
   215	            process::exit(128 + sig);

I see a potential issue. When we're in foreground mode and receive a signal, we send it to the specific child PID. However, when not in foreground mode (which is the default), we're sending to process group 0, which is the current process group. Let me trace through the logic:

1. At the start of `timeout()`, if `!foreground`, we call `setpgid(0, 0)` which creates a new process group with the timeout process as the leader.
2. The child process inherits this process group.
3. When we call `kill(0, sig)`, it sends the signal to all processes in the current process group, which includes both the timeout process and its children.

Wait, that's an issue! When we send a signal to process group 0, it will also hit the timeout process itself, potentially causing recursive signal handling. Let me check GNU timeout's behavior more carefully.

   241	fn send_signal(process: &mut Child, signal: usize, foreground: bool) {
   242	    // NOTE: GNU timeout doesn't check for errors of signal.
   243	    // The subprocess might have exited just after the timeout.
   244	    // Sending a signal now would return "No such process", but we should still try to kill the children.
   245	    if foreground {
   246	        let _ = process.send_signal(signal);
   247	    } else {
   248	        let _ = process.send_signal_group(signal);
   249	        let kill_signal = signal_by_name_or_value("KILL").unwrap();
   250	        let continued_signal = signal_by_name_or_value("CONT").unwrap();
   251	        if signal != kill_signal && signal != continued_signal {
   252	            _ = process.send_signal_group(continued_signal);
   253	        }
   254	    }
   255	}

   103	    fn send_signal_group(&mut self, signal: usize) -> io::Result<()> {
   104	        // Ignore the signal, so we don't go into a signal loop.
   105	        if unsafe { libc::signal(signal as i32, libc::SIG_IGN) } != 0 {
   106	            return Err(io::Error::last_os_error());
   107	        }
   108	        if unsafe { libc::kill(0, signal as i32) } == 0 {
   109	            Ok(())
   110	        } else {
   111	            Err(io::Error::last_os_error())
   112	        }

///
/// This function sets up handlers that will send signals to the child process
/// and then exit when the timeout process receives termination signals.
fn setup_signal_handlers(child_pid: i32, foreground: bool) -> std::io::Result<()> {
    use signal_hook::consts::signal::*;
    use signal_hook::iterator::Signals;
    
    // Create a signal set for the signals we want to catch
    let mut signals = Signals::new(&[SIGTERM, SIGINT, SIGHUP, SIGQUIT])?;
    
    // Spawn a thread to handle signals
    std::thread::spawn(move || {
        for sig in signals.forever() {
            // Forward the signal to the child process or process group
            if foreground {
                unsafe {
                    libc::kill(child_pid, sig);
                }
            } else {
                // Send to the entire process group
                unsafe {
                    libc::kill(0, sig);
                }
            }
            // Exit immediately after forwarding the signal
            // This matches GNU timeout behavior
            process::exit(128 + sig);
        }
    });
    
    Ok(())
}' --new_str '/// Set up signal handlers to forward termination signals to the child process.
///
/// This function sets up handlers that will send signals to the child process
/// and then exit when the timeout process receives termination signals.
fn setup_signal_handlers(child_pid: i32, foreground: bool) -> std::io::Result<()> {
    use signal_hook::consts::signal::*;
    use signal_hook::iterator::Signals;
    
    // Create a signal set for the signals we want to catch
    let mut signals = Signals::new(&[SIGTERM, SIGINT, SIGHUP, SIGQUIT])?;
    
    // Spawn a thread to handle signals
    std::thread::spawn(move || {
        for sig in signals.forever() {
            // Forward the signal to the child process or process group
            if foreground {
                unsafe {
                    libc::kill(child_pid, sig);
                }
            } else {
                // Ignore the signal in our process to avoid signal loop,
                // then send to the entire process group
                unsafe {
                    libc::signal(sig, libc::SIG_IGN);
                    libc::kill(0, sig);
                }
            }
            // Exit immediately after forwarding the signal
            // This matches GNU timeout behavior
            process::exit(128 + sig);
        }
    });
    
    Ok(())
}'

#!/bin/bash

echo "Additional edge case tests"

# Test 1: Child exits normally before signal
echo "Test 1: Child exits before signal arrives"
/testbed/target/debug/timeout 10 sleep 0.1 &
PID=$!
sleep 0.2
kill -TERM $PID 2>/dev/null
wait $PID 2>/dev/null
EXIT_CODE=$?
if [ $EXIT_CODE -eq 0 ]; then
    echo "✓ Test 1 passed: Normal exit code preserved"
else
    echo "✗ Test 1 failed: Exit code is $EXIT_CODE instead of 0"
fi

# Test 2: Signal while using --preserve-status
echo ""
echo "Test 2: Signal with --preserve-status"
/testbed/target/debug/timeout --preserve-status 42 sleep 42 &
PID=$!
sleep 0.5
SLEEP_PID=$(pgrep -P $PID sleep || echo "")
if [ -n "$SLEEP_PID" ]; then
    kill -TERM $PID
    sleep 0.5
    if ps -p $SLEEP_PID > /dev/null 2>&1; then
        echo "✗ Test 2 failed: Sleep still running"
        kill -9 $SLEEP_PID 2>/dev/null
    else
        echo "✓ Test 2 passed: Sleep terminated with --preserve-status"
    fi
else
    echo "✗ Test 2 failed: Could not find sleep"
fi

# Test 3: Signal with --verbose
echo ""
echo "Test 3: Signal with --verbose"
/testbed/target/debug/timeout --verbose 42 sleep 42 &
PID=$!
sleep 0.5

    sleep 0.5
    if ps -p $SLEEP_PID > /dev/null 2>&1; then
        echo "✗ Test 3 failed: Sleep still running"
        kill -9 $SLEEP_PID 2>/dev/null
    else
        echo "✓ Test 3 passed: Sleep terminated with --verbose"
    fi
else
    echo "✗ Test 3 failed: Could not find sleep"
fi

# Test 4: Test SIGQUIT signal
echo ""
echo "Test 4: SIGQUIT signal handling"
/testbed/target/debug/timeout 42 sleep 42 &
PID=$!
sleep 0.5

if [ -n "$SLEEP_PID" ]; then
    kill -QUIT $PID 2>/dev/null
    sleep 0.5
    if ps -p $SLEEP_PID > /dev/null 2>&1; then
        echo "✗ Test 4 failed: Sleep still running after QUIT"
        kill -9 $SLEEP_PID 2>/dev/null
    else
        echo "✓ Test 4 passed: Sleep terminated after QUIT"
    fi

#!/bin/bash
echo "Testing QUIT signal"
/testbed/target/debug/timeout 42 sleep 42 &
PID=$!
echo "Started timeout with PID $PID"
sleep 0.5

SLEEP_PID=$(pgrep -P $PID sleep || echo "")
echo "Sleep PID: $SLEEP_PID"

if [ -n "$SLEEP_PID" ]; then
    echo "Sending QUIT signal..."
    kill -QUIT $PID
    sleep 1
    
    echo "Checking if processes are still running..."
    ps -p $PID && echo "Timeout is still running" || echo "Timeout exited"
    ps -p $SLEEP_PID && echo "Sleep is still running" || echo "Sleep exited"
    
    # Cleanup
    kill -9 $PID $SLEEP_PID 2>/dev/null
fi
EOF

#!/bin/bash
echo "Testing QUIT signal with strace"
strace -e signal -f /testbed/target/debug/timeout 42 sleep 42 &
PID=$!
echo "Started timeout with PID $PID"
sleep 1

SLEEP_PID=$(pgrep -P $PID sleep || echo "")
echo "Sleep PID: $SLEEP_PID"

if [ -n "$SLEEP_PID" ]; then
    echo "Sending QUIT signal to $PID..."
    kill -QUIT $PID
    sleep 1
    
    echo "Checking if processes are still running..."
    ps -p $SLEEP_PID && echo "Sleep is still running - BUG" || echo "Sleep exited - GOOD"
    
    # Cleanup
    kill -9 $PID $SLEEP_PID 2>/dev/null
fi
EOF

Let me think about this differently. When SIGQUIT is sent to the timeout process, the signal handler thread should receive it and forward it. But the issue is that SIGQUIT has special behavior - it generates a core dump. Let me check if the issue is that the timeout process is exiting with SIGQUIT before the signal handler can process it.

Actually, I think I see the issue. When we exit with `process::exit(128 + sig)`, we're doing a normal exit, not a signal-based exit. So the shell sees it as a normal termination. But the key issue is that the child process is still running.

#!/bin/bash

echo "Manual QUIT test"

# Start a simple sleep in background
sleep 100 &
SLEEP_PID=$!
echo "Started sleep with PID $SLEEP_PID"

# Send QUIT to it
echo "Sending QUIT to sleep..."
kill -QUIT $SLEEP_PID
sleep 0.5

# Check if it's running
if ps -p $SLEEP_PID > /dev/null 2>&1; then
    echo "Sleep is still running after QUIT - this shouldn't happen!"
    kill -9 $SLEEP_PID
else
    echo "Sleep terminated after QUIT - expected behavior"
fi

echo ""
echo "Now testing with timeout"
/testbed/target/debug/timeout 42 sleep 100 &
TIMEOUT_PID=$!
sleep 0.5

CHILD_PID=$(pgrep -P $TIMEOUT_PID sleep)
echo "Timeout PID: $TIMEOUT_PID, Child PID: $CHILD_PID"

echo "Sending QUIT to timeout..."
kill -QUIT $TIMEOUT_PID
sleep 1

echo "Checking status..."
if ps -p $TIMEOUT_PID > /dev/null 2>&1; then
    echo "Timeout still running"
    kill -9 $TIMEOUT_PID 2>/dev/null
else
    echo "Timeout exited"
fi

if ps -p $CHILD_PID > /dev/null 2>&1; then
    echo "Child still running - BUG!"
    kill -9 $CHILD_PID 2>/dev/null
else
    echo "Child exited - GOOD"
fi
EOF

So GNU timeout exits with code 0 when the child completes successfully, even if you try to send TERM to it afterwards (which fails because it's already gone). The issue in test 1 is that we're trying to send a signal to a process that has already exited, and then we're checking the exit code. The fact that we get 143 suggests that maybe the timeout process hasn't fully exited yet when we send the signal. This is actually not part of the PR requirements - the PR is about orphaned child processes, not exit codes when racing with signals.

Let me verify that our main goal is achieved - no orphaned processes:

🎬 ACTION
echo "=== Final Comprehensive Test ==="
echo ""
echo "Ensuring no orphaned processes remain after TERM signal"
echo ""

# Clean up any existing processes
pkill -9 -f "sleep 42" 2>/dev/null
sleep 0.5

# Test scenario from PR: Multiple timeout processes terminated by TERM
echo "Starting 10 timeout processes..."
for i in {1..10}; do
    /testbed/target/debug/timeout 60 sleep 60 &
    sleep 0.05
done

echo "Waiting for processes to start..."
sleep 1

BEFORE_COUNT=$(pgrep -f "sleep 60" | wc -l)
echo "Sleep processes before TERM: $BEFORE_COUNT"

echo "Sending TERM to all timeout processes..."
pkill -TERM -f "^/testbed/target/debug/timeout"
sleep 2

AFTER_COUNT=$(pgrep -f "sleep 60" | wc -l)
echo "Sleep processes after TERM: $AFTER_COUNT"

# Cleanup
pkill -9 -f "sleep 60" 2>/dev/null
pkill -9 -f "^/testbed/target/debug/timeout" 2>/dev/null

if [ $AFTER_COUNT -eq 0 ]; then
    echo ""
    echo "✓✓✓ SUCCESS: No orphaned processes! PR issue is resolved! ✓✓✓"
    exit 0
else
    echo ""
    echo "✗✗✗ FAILURE: $AFTER_COUNT orphaned processes remain! ✗✗✗"
    exit 1
fi

+/// Set up signal handlers to forward termination signals to the child process.
+///
+/// This function sets up handlers that will send signals to the child process
+/// and then exit when the timeout process receives termination signals.
+fn setup_signal_handlers(child_pid: i32, foreground: bool) -> std::io::Result<()> {
+    use signal_hook::consts::signal::*;
+    use signal_hook::iterator::Signals;
+    
+    // Create a signal set for the signals we want to catch
+    let mut signals = Signals::new(&[SIGTERM, SIGINT, SIGHUP, SIGQUIT])?;
+    
+    // Spawn a thread to handle signals
+    std::thread::spawn(move || {
+        for sig in signals.forever() {
+            // Forward the signal to the child process or process group
+            if foreground {
+                unsafe {
+                    libc::kill(child_pid, sig);
+                }
+            } else {
+                // Send to the entire process group
+                // Note: signal-hook already caught the signal, so we won't get into a loop
+                unsafe {
+                    libc::kill(0, sig);
+                }
+            }
+            // Exit immediately after forwarding the signal
+            // This matches GNU timeout behavior
+            process::exit(128 + sig);
+        }
+    });
+    
+    Ok(())
+}
+
+
+

diff --git a/test_simple.sh b/test_simple.sh
new file mode 100755
index 000000000..f10e0b7b8
--- /dev/null
+++ b/test_simple.sh
@@ -0,0 +1,70 @@
+#!/bin/bash
+
+echo "Testing GNU timeout behavior (reference)..."
+# Test if GNU timeout is available
+if command -v /usr/bin/timeout &> /dev/null; then
+    echo "Starting GNU timeout with sleep 42..."
+    /usr/bin/timeout 42 sleep 42 &
+    TIMEOUT_PID=$!
+    sleep 0.5  # Give it time to start
+    
+    # Find the child sleep process
+    SLEEP_PID=$(pgrep -P $TIMEOUT_PID sleep || echo "")
+    
+    if [ -n "$SLEEP_PID" ]; then
+        echo "Timeout PID: $TIMEOUT_PID, Sleep PID: $SLEEP_PID"
+        echo "Sending TERM signal to timeout..."
+        kill -TERM $TIMEOUT_PID
+        sleep 0.5
+        
+        # Check if sleep is still running
+        if ps -p $SLEEP_PID > /dev/null 2>&1; then
+            echo "❌ GNU timeout: Sleep process is still running!"
+            kill -9 $SLEEP_PID 2>/dev/null || true
+        else
+            echo "✓ GNU timeout: Sleep process was terminated correctly"
+        fi
+    else
+        echo "Could not find child sleep process"
+    fi
+    
+    # Cleanup
+    kill -9 $TIMEOUT_PID 2>/dev/null || true
+fi
+
+echo ""
+echo "Testing uutils timeout behavior..."
+cd /testbed
+echo "Starting uutils timeout with sleep 42..."
+./target/debug/timeout 42 sleep 42 &
+TIMEOUT_PID=$!
+sleep 0.5  # Give it time to start
+
+# Find the child sleep process
+SLEEP_PID=$(pgrep -P $TIMEOUT_PID sleep || echo "")
+
+if [ -n "$SLEEP_PID" ]; then
+    echo "Timeout PID: $TIMEOUT_PID, Sleep PID: $SLEEP_PID"
+    echo "Sending TERM signal to timeout..."
+    kill -TERM $TIMEOUT_PID
+    sleep 0.5
+    
+    # Check if sleep is still running
+    if ps -p $SLEEP_PID > /dev/null 2>&1; then
+        echo "❌ UUTILS timeout: Sleep process is still running (BUG CONFIRMED!)"
+        # Check who the parent is now
+        PPID=$(ps -o ppid= -p $SLEEP_PID | tr -d ' ')
+        echo "   Sleep process parent PID is now: $PPID"
+        kill -9 $SLEEP_PID 2>/dev/null || true
+    else
+        echo "✓ UUTILS timeout: Sleep process was terminated correctly"
+    fi
+else
+    echo "Could not find child sleep process"
+fi
+
+# Cleanup
+kill -9 $TIMEOUT_PID 2>/dev/null || true
+
+echo ""
+echo "Test complete!"

+    echo "Starting GNU timeout with sleep 42..."

+    TIMEOUT_PID=$!

+

+

+        echo "Timeout PID: $TIMEOUT_PID, Sleep PID: $SLEEP_PID"
+        echo "Sending TERM signal to timeout..."
